31 // Type: UInt32 -- VT_UI4
32 // FormatID: (FMTID_AudioSummaryInformation) 64440490-4C8B-11D1-8B70-080036B11A03, 7 (PIDASI_CHANNEL_COUNT)
33 //
34 // Indicates the channel count for the audio file. Values: 1 (mono), 2 (stereo).

799 //
800 // This is the file extension of the file based item, including the leading period.
801 //
802 // If System.FileName is VT_EMPTY, then this property should be too. Otherwise, it should be derived
803 // appropriately by the data source from System.FileName. If System.FileName does not have a file
804 // extension, this value should be VT_EMPTY.
805 //
806 // To obtain the type of any item (including an item that is not a file), use System.ItemType.
807 //
808 // Example values:
809 //
810 // If the path is... The property value is...
811 // ----------------- ------------------------
812 // "c:\foo\bar\hello.txt" ".txt"
813 // "\\server\share\mydir\goodnews.doc" ".doc"
814 // "\\server\share\numbers.xls" ".xls"
815 // "\\server\share\folder" VT_EMPTY
816 // "c:\foo\MyFolder" VT_EMPTY
817 // [desktop] VT_EMPTY
818 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_FileExtension, 0xE4F10A3C, 0x49E6, 0x405D, 0x82, 0x88, 0xA2, 0x3B, 0xD4, 0xEE, 0xAA, 0x6C, 100);

828 // Name: System.FileName -- PKEY_FileName
829 // Type: String -- VT_LPWSTR (For variants: VT_BSTR)
830 // FormatID: 41CF5AE0-F75A-4806-BD87-59C7D9248EB9, 100
831 //
832 // This is the file name (including extension) of the file.
833 //
834 // It is possible that the item might not exist on a filesystem (ie, it may not be opened
835 // using CreateFile). Nonetheless, if the item is represented as a file from the logical sense
836 // (and its name follows standard Win32 file-naming syntax), then the data source should emit this property.
837 //
838 // If an item is not a file, then the value for this property is VT_EMPTY. See
839 // System.ItemNameDisplay.
840 //
841 // This has the same value as System.ParsingName for items that are provided by the Shell's file folder.
842 //
843 // Example values:
844 //
845 // If the path is... The property value is...
846 // ----------------- ------------------------
847 // "c:\foo\bar\hello.txt" "hello.txt"
848 // "\\server\share\mydir\goodnews.doc" "goodnews.doc"
849 // "\\server\share\numbers.xls" "numbers.xls"
850 // "c:\foo\MyFolder" "MyFolder"
851 // (email message) VT_EMPTY
852 // (song on portable device) "song.wma"
853 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_FileName, 0x41CF5AE0, 0xF75A, 0x4806, 0xBD, 0x87, 0x59, 0xC7, 0xD9, 0x24, 0x8E, 0xB9, 100);

1088 
1089 // Name: System.ItemName -- PKEY_ItemName
1090 // Type: String -- VT_LPWSTR (For variants: VT_BSTR)
1091 // FormatID: 6B8DA074-3B5C-43BC-886F-0A2CDCE00B6F, 100
1092 //
1093 // This is the base-name of the System.ItemNameDisplay.
1094 //
1095 // If the item is a file this property
1096 // includes the extension in all cases, and will be localized if a localized name is available.
1097 //
1098 // If the item is a message, then the value of this property does not include the forwarding or
1099 // reply prefixes (see System.ItemNamePrefix).
1100 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_ItemName, 0x6B8DA074, 0x3B5C, 0x43BC, 0x88, 0x6F, 0x0A, 0x2C, 0xDC, 0xE0, 0x0B, 0x6F, 100);
1101 
1102 // Name: System.ItemNameDisplay -- PKEY_ItemNameDisplay
1103 // Type: String -- VT_LPWSTR (For variants: VT_BSTR)
1104 // FormatID: (FMTID_Storage) B725F130-47EF-101A-A5F1-02608C9EEBAC, 10 (PID_STG_NAME)
1105 //
1106 // This is the display name in "most complete" form. This is the best effort unique representation
1107 // of the name of an item that makes sense for end users to read. It is the concatentation of
1108 // System.ItemNamePrefix and System.ItemName.
1109 //
1110 // If the item is a file this property
1111 // includes the extension in all cases, and will be localized if a localized name is available.
1112 //
1113 // There are acceptable cases when System.FileName is not VT_EMPTY, yet the value of this property
1114 // is completely different. Email messages are a key example. If the item is an email message,
1115 // the item name is likely the subject. In that case, the value must be the concatenation of the
1116 // System.ItemNamePrefix and System.ItemName. Since the value of System.ItemNamePrefix excludes
1117 // any trailing whitespace, the concatenation must include a whitespace when generating System.ItemNameDisplay.
1118 //
1119 // Note that this property is not guaranteed to be unique, but the idea is to promote the most likely
1120 // candidate that can be unique and also makes sense for end users. For example, for documents, you
1121 // might think about using System.Title as the System.ItemNameDisplay, but in practice the title of
1122 // the documents may not be useful or unique enough to be of value as the sole System.ItemNameDisplay.
1123 // Instead, providing the value of System.FileName as the value of System.ItemNameDisplay is a better
1124 // candidate. In Windows Mail, the emails are stored in the file system as .eml files and the
1125 // System.FileName for those files are not human-friendly as they contain GUIDs. In this example,
1126 // promoting System.Subject as System.ItemNameDisplay makes more sense.
1127 //
1128 // Compatibility notes:
1129 //
1130 // Shell folder implementations on Vista: use PKEY_ItemNameDisplay for the name column when
1131 // you want Explorer to call ISF::GetDisplayNameOf(SHGDN_NORMAL) to get the value of the name. Use
1132 // another PKEY (like PKEY_ItemName) when you want Explorer to call either the folder's property store or
1133 // ISF2::GetDetailsEx in order to get the value of the name.
1134 //
1135 // Shell folder implementations on XP: the first column needs to be the name column, and Explorer
1136 // will call ISF::GetDisplayNameOf to get the value of the name. The PKEY/SCID does not matter.
1137 //
1138 // Example values:
1139 //
1140 // File: "hello.txt"
1141 // Message: "Re: Let's talk about Tom's argyle socks!"
1142 // Device folder: "song.wma"
1143 // Folder: "Documents"
1144 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_ItemNameDisplay, 0xB725F130, 0x47EF, 0x101A, 0xA5, 0xF1, 0x02, 0x60, 0x8C, 0x9E, 0xEB, 0xAC, 10);
1145 
1146 // Name: System.ItemNamePrefix -- PKEY_ItemNamePrefix
1147 // Type: String -- VT_LPWSTR (For variants: VT_BSTR)
1148 // FormatID: D7313FF1-A77A-401C-8C99-3DBDD68ADD36, 100
1149 //
1150 // This is the prefix of an item, used for email messages.
1151 // where the subject begins with "Re:" which is the prefix.
1152 //
1153 // If the item is a file, then the value of this property is VT_EMPTY.
1154 //
1155 // If the item is a message, then the value of this property is the forwarding or reply
1156 // prefixes (including delimiting colon, but no whitespace), or VT_EMPTY if there is no prefix.
1157 //
1158 // Example values:
1159 //
1160 // System.ItemNamePrefix System.ItemName System.ItemNameDisplay
1161 // --------------------- ------------------- ----------------------
1162 // VT_EMPTY "Great day" "Great day"
1163 // "Re:" "Great day" "Re: Great day"
1164 // "Fwd: " "Monthly budget" "Fwd: Monthly budget"
1165 // VT_EMPTY "accounts.xls" "accounts.xls"
1166 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_ItemNamePrefix, 0xD7313FF1, 0xA77A, 0x401C, 0x8C, 0x99, 0x3D, 0xBD, 0xD6, 0x8A, 0xDD, 0x36, 100);
1167 
1168 // Name: System.ItemParticipants -- PKEY_ItemParticipants
1169 // Type: Multivalue String -- VT_VECTOR | VT_LPWSTR (For variants: VT_ARRAY | VT_BSTR)

1171 //
1172 // This is the generic list of people associated with an item and who contributed
1173 // to the item.
1174 //
1175 // For example, this is the combination of people in the To list, Cc list and
1176 // sender of an email message.
1177 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_ItemParticipants, 0xD4D0AA16, 0x9948, 0x41A4, 0xAA, 0x85, 0xD9, 0x7F, 0xF9, 0x64, 0x69, 0x93, 100);
1178 
1179 // Name: System.ItemPathDisplay -- PKEY_ItemPathDisplay

1229 // Name: System.ItemType -- PKEY_ItemType

1231 // FormatID: (FMTID_ShellDetails) 28636AA6-953D-11D2-B5D6-00C04FD918D0, 11

1256 
1257 // Name: System.ItemTypeText -- PKEY_ItemTypeText
1258 // Type: String -- VT_LPWSTR (For variants: VT_BSTR)

1260 //
1261 // This is the user friendly type name of the item. This is not intended to be
1262 // programmatically parsed.
1263 //
1264 // If System.ItemType is VT_EMPTY, the value of this property is also VT_EMPTY.
1265 //
1266 // If the item is a file, the value of this property is the same as if you passed the
1267 // file's System.ItemType value to PSFormatForDisplay.
1268 //
1269 // This property should not be confused with System.Kind, where System.Kind is a high-level
1270 // user friendly kind name. For example, for a document, System.Kind = "Document" and
1271 // System.Item.Type = ".doc" and System.Item.TypeText = "Microsoft Word Document"
1272 //
1273 // Example values:
1274 //
1275 // If the path is... The property value is...

1278 // "\\server\share\mydir\goodnews.doc" "Microsoft Word Document"
1279 // "\\server\share\folder" "File Folder"
1280 // "c:\foo\MyFolder" "File Folder"
1281 // "/Mailbox Account/Inbox/'Re: Hello!'" "Outlook E-Mail Message"
1282 DEFINE_PROPERTYKEY(PKEY_ItemTypeText, 0xB725F130, 0x47EF, 0x101A, 0xA5, 0xF1, 0x02, 0x60, 0x8C, 0x9E, 0xEB, 0xAC, 4);

1284 // Name: System.ItemUrl -- PKEY_ItemUrl
